HIPAA COMPLIANT MEDICAL AUTHORIZATION 
(Authorization to Release Protected Health Care Information) 
To: 
Dear Medical Records Clerk: 
I have retained The Whaley Law Firm, PSC to represent me in matters related to an injury sustained due to a third parties’ negligence. Please 
forward a copy of any & all records not previously provided to The Whaley Law Firm upon request. 
Pursuant to the Health Insurance Portability & Accountability Act (HIPAA) Privacy Regulations, 45 CFR 164.508, the provider listed above is 
hereby authorized to release to The Whaley Law Firm, PSC or any of their representatives, all medical records, including but not limited to: Office 
Notes, History, Physical, Consultation Notes, Discharge Summaries, Orders, Progress Notes, Laboratory Results, Nurses’ Notes, Emergency Room 
Records, Operative Reports, In-Patient Records and films of X-Rays, MRIs, CT Scans, or PET Scans, Pharmacy and Drug Records, Medical Bills 
and Health Insurance Information, Medicaid/Medicare Records, concerning ANY medical treatment that I have received from you and/or at your 
facility, as well as ALL such records which you keep in the regular course of business that are found in my medical record file. 
I hereby authorize the release of ANY & ALL records regarding mental health, psychiatric (other than psychotherapy notes, which must be 
requested under separate authorization), Chemical Dependency or HIV. 
A photostatic copy hereof shall be as valid as the original. 
I hereby authorize a FREE COPY of my medical records pursuant to KRS 422.317 be sent to the extent I have not already requested my one free 
copy. 
The purpose of this authorization and request is to permit my attorney to obtain ALL medical information pertaining to my physical and mental 
condition(s). This authorization expires in three (3) years from the date of the signature. The aforementioned expiration date has not passed, as 
this matter is on-going. I hereby authorize The Whaley Law Firm, PSC. to speak to my healthcare providers privately or to take the testimony at 
deposition and/or trial as may be requested. 
I have the right to revoke this authorization in writing by providing a signed, written notice of revocation to the healthcare provider listed above 
and to The Whaley Law Firm, PSC. I understand that there are exceptions to the right to revoke. Among the exceptions to the right to revoke are 
that an individual may not revoke an authorization to the extent that the covered entity has taken action in reliance thereon. Medical Providers 
may not condition treatment or payment on whether the above-listed patient executes this authorization. The information disclosed pursuant to 
this authorization may be subject to re-disclosure and no longer protected by the privacy regulations promulgated pursuant to the Health Insurance 
Portability and Accountability Act (HIPAA) 
_________________________________

(Authorization to Release Protected Health Care Information)
KORT Elizabethtown PT
To: [PHONE-388]

Dear Medical Records Clerk:
I have retained The Whaley Law Firm, PSC to represent me in matters related to an injury sustained due to a third parties' negligence. Please
forward a copy of any & all records not previously provided to The Whaley Law Firm upon request.
Pursuant to the Health Insurance Portability & Accountability Act (HIPAA) Privacy Regulations, 45 CFR 164.508, the provider listed above is
hereby authorized to release to The Whaley Law Firm, PSC or any of their representatives, all medical records, including but not limited to: Office
Notes, History, Physical, Consultation Notes, Discharge Summaries, Orders, Progress Notes, Laboratory Results, Nurses' Notes, Emergency Room
Records, Operative Reports, In-Patient Records and films of X-Rays, MRIs, CT Scans, or PET Scans, Pharmacy and Drug Records, Medical Bills
and Health Insurance Information, Medicaid/Medicare Records, concerning ANY medical treatment that I have received from you and/or at your
facility, as well as ALL such records which you keep in the regular course of business that are found in my medical record file.
I hereby authorize the release of ANY & ALL records regarding mental health, psychiatric (other than psychotherapy notes, which must be
requested under separate authorization), Chemical Dependency or HIV.
A photostatic copy hereof shall be as valid as the original.
I hereby authorize a FREE COPY of my medical records pursuant to KRS 422.317 be sent to the extent I have not already requested my one free
copy.
The purpose of this authorization and request is to permit my attorney to obtain ALL medical information pertaining to my physical and mental
condition(s). This authorization expires in three (3) years from the date of the signature. The aforementioned expiration date has not passed, as
this matter is on-going. I hereby authorize The Whaley Law Firm, PSC. to speak to my healthcare providers privately or to take the testimony at
deposition and/or trial as may be requested.
I have the right to revoke this authorization in writing by providing a signed, written notice of revocation to the healthcare provider listed above
and to The Whaley Law Firm, PSC. I understand that there are exceptions to the right to revoke. Among the exceptions to the right to revoke are
that an individual may not revoke an authorization to the extent that the covered entity has taken action in reliance thereon. Medical Providers may not condition treatment or payment on whether the above-listed patient executes this authorization. Diagnoses
Initial Evaluation 
Left M54.12 Radiculopathy, cervical region
Spine
M54.16 Radiculopathy, lumbar region
M54.6 Pain in thoracic spine
General Information
Pt. reports being involved in MVA May 30 during which he was hit on the side by an ambulance. States he had pre-existing issues
with L shoulder and neck/LUE, and this exacerbated symptoms greatly. Had 100 lbs. land on his head and L shoulder in 2002
while working previous job, and had visual disturbances since then. States he had SLAP repair L shoulder in 2014 and vein
procedure done on L arm, which was slightly successful, but still have significant weakness throughout LUE and limited motion L
shoulder. Have "blackouts" when turning head too quickly. Also been having intermittent radiating pain and N/T down LLE into
big toe. A good night sleep has been ~2 hours. Works as a baker. Very difficult driving due to neck rotation.
Patient has not been identified as a fall risk at the time of this evaluation.
Summary List: Significant Medical DX/Conditions: Present: Asthma, Back injury

Left Spine

General Information
Pt. reports being involved in MVA May 30 during which he was hit on the side by an ambulance. States he had pre-existing issues
with L shoulder and neck/LUE, and this exacerbated symptoms greatly. Had 100 lbs. land on his head and L shoulder in 2002
while working previous job, and had visual disturbances since then. States he had SLAP repair L shoulder in 2014 and vein
procedure done on L arm, which was slightly successful, but still have significant weakness throughout LUE and limited motion L
shoulder. Have "blackouts" when turning head too quickly. Also been having intermittent radiating pain and N/T down LLE into
big toe. A good night sleep has been ~2 hours. Works as a baker. Very difficult driving due to neck rotation.
Patient has not been identified as a fall risk at the time of this evaluation.

Assessment
Jimmy Ferguson is a 50 year old male who presents to clinic with c/o acute exacerbation of chronic neck pain with LUE weakness,
chronic L shoulder pain, and acute LBP with radiating LLE pain and N/T onset MVA 5/30/24. Demonstrates significantly decreased
gross C-spine AROM, most noted with rotation to L. Positive ULTT#1. Demonstrates significantly decreased gross L shoulder
A/PROM and LUE strength.
Positive LLE neurotension testing. Lumbar traction exacerbates back pain. Prone positioning exacerbates local back pain.
Demonstrates significantly decreased gross LLE strength relative to RLE. Significantly decreased trunk stability in all planes of
motion.
The patient requires skilled physical therapy to address the problems identified, and to achieve the individualized patient goals as
outlined in the problems and goals section of this evaluation. Overall rehabilitation potential is good.
The patient was educated regarding their diagnosis, prognosis, related pathology & plan of care. The patient demonstrates a
good understanding of the risks, benefits, precautions/contraindications, & prognosis of their skilled rehabilitation program.

M54.16 Radiculopathy, lumbar region
M54.6 Pain in thoracic spine
General Information
Pt. reports being involved in MVA May 30 during which he was hit on the side by an ambulance. States he had pre-existing issues
with L shoulder and neck/LUE, and this exacerbated symptoms greatly. Had 100 lbs. land on his head and L shoulder in 2002
while working previous job, and had visual disturbances since then. States he had SLAP repair L shoulder in 2014 and vein
procedure done on L arm, which was slightly successful, but still have significant weakness throughout LUE and limited motion L
shoulder. Have "blackouts" when turning head too quickly. Also been having intermittent radiating pain and N/T down LLE into
big toe. A good night sleep has been ~2 hours. Works as a baker. Very difficult driving due to neck rotation.
Patient has not been identified as a fall risk at the time of this evaluation.

Daily Note 
Left M54.12 Radiculopathy, cervical region
Spine
M54.16 Radiculopathy, lumbar region
M54.6 Pain in thoracic spine
General Information
Pt. reports being involved in MVA May 30 during which he was hit on the side by an ambulance. States he had pre-existing issues
with L shoulder and neck/LUE, and this exacerbated symptoms greatly. Had 100 lbs. land on his head and L shoulder in 2002
while working previous job, and had visual disturbances since then. States he had SLAP repair L shoulder in 2014 and vein
procedure done on L arm, which was slightly successful, but still have significant weakness throughout LUE and limited motion L
shoulder. Have "blackouts" when turning head too quickly. Also been having intermittent radiating pain and N/T down LLE into
big toe. A good night sleep has been ~2 hours. Works as a baker. Very difficult driving due to neck rotation.
Patient has not been identified as a fall risk at the time of this evaluation.
Summary List: Significant Medical DX/Conditions: Present: Asthma, Back injury
Subjective Examination
Left Spine
Mechanism of Injury: MVA May 30 2024
Mini-open labral debridement 2014
100 lbs. dropped on head from >20 feet. in 2002

Daily Note 
Left M54.12 Radiculopathy, cervical region
Spine
M54.16 Radiculopathy, lumbar region
M54.6 Pain in thoracic spine
General Information
Pt. reports being involved in MVA May 30 during which he was hit on the side by an ambulance. States he had pre-existing issues
with L shoulder and neck/LUE, and this exacerbated symptoms greatly. Had 100 lbs. land on his head and L shoulder in 2002
while working previous job, and had visual disturbances since then. States he had SLAP repair L shoulder in 2014 and vein
procedure done on L arm, which was slightly successful, but still have significant weakness throughout LUE and limited motion L
shoulder. Have "blackouts" when turning head too quickly. Also been having intermittent radiating pain and N/T down LLE into
big toe. A good night sleep has been ~2 hours. Works as a baker. Very difficult driving due to neck rotation.
Patient has not been identified as a fall risk at the time of this evaluation.
Summary List: Significant Medical DX/Conditions: Present: Asthma, Back injury
Subjective Examination
Left Spine
Mechanism of Injury: MVA May 30 2024
Mini-open labral debridement 2014
100 lbs. dropped on head from >20 feet. in 2002

Assessment
Evaluation Components: Jimmy Ferguson has attended 6 treatment sessions including evaluation for acute exacerbation of
chronic neck pain with LUE weakness, and chronic L shoulder pain onset MVA 5/30/24. Secondary c/o acute LBP with radiating
LLE pain and N/T. Not reporting a significant change in neck pain and reports multiple events since MVA during which his legs
give out when turning head quickly. Getting very little sleep still. Has made fair progress with C-spine rotation to L, L shoulder
AROM, and gross LUE strength with arm in neutral. Due to persistent high pain levels, patient's pre-existing history of LUE
dysfunction, and multiple "blackout" events, recommend he receive updated MRI of C-spine and L shoulder. Would also benefit
from consult with orthopedist regarding L shoulder and f/u with Dr. Jackson regarding neurological symptoms.
Recommendations: Skilled Intervention: Required To: Decrease Pain.
The patient was educated regarding their diagnosis, prognosis, related pathology & plan of care. The patient demonstrates a
good understanding of the risks, benefits, precautions/contraindications, & prognosis of their skilled rehabilitation program.
Recommendations: Skilled Intervention:
 • Required To: Improve Function. Improve Motor Control. Increase Range of Motion. Increase Strength.

Daily Note 
Left M54.12 Radiculopathy, cervical region
Spine
M54.16 Radiculopathy, lumbar region
M54.6 Pain in thoracic spine
General Information
Pt. reports being involved in MVA May 30 during which he was hit on the side by an ambulance. States he had pre-existing issues
with L shoulder and neck/LUE, and this exacerbated symptoms greatly. Had 100 lbs. land on his head and L shoulder in 2002
while working previous job, and had visual disturbances since then. States he had SLAP repair L shoulder in 2014 and vein
procedure done on L arm, which was slightly successful, but still have significant weakness throughout LUE and limited motion L
shoulder. Have "blackouts" when turning head too quickly. Also been having intermittent radiating pain and N/T down LLE into
big toe. A good night sleep has been ~2 hours. Works as a baker. Very difficult driving due to neck rotation.
Patient has not been identified as a fall risk at the time of this evaluation.
Summary List: Significant Medical DX/Conditions: Present: Asthma, Back injury
Subjective Examination
Left Spine
Mechanism of Injury: MVA May 30 2024
Mini-open labral debridement 2014
100 lbs. dropped on head from >20 feet. in 2002

Chief Complaint: Pain: Severity:
 • Current 9/10
 • At Best 9/10
 • At Worst 9/10

 • Driving/Traveling Painful turning head
 • Housework- Heavy Unable to Perform
 • Sitting Increases back pain
 • Standing Increases back pain after extended period of time

temporary pain relief.
10/2: Pt. states he's not sleeping much.
10/4: Pt. states if he sleeps in recliner, he wakes up with a severe muscle spasm in neck. Can't get comfortable in bed either.
10/9: Pt. states he had another event in past few days during which he turned quickly and legs gave out on him.
10/11: Pt. states LBP is mostly left-sided and at times radiates down LLE. This can occur with quick rotation or prolonged sitting.

Daily Note
Diagnoses
Left M54.12 Radiculopathy, cervical region M54.16 Radiculopathy, lumbar region
Spine
M54.6 Pain in thoracic spine
General Information
Pt. reports being involved in MVA May 30 during which he was hit on the side by an ambulance. States he had pre-existing issues
with L shoulder and neck/LUE, and this exacerbated symptoms greatly. Had 100 lbs. land on his head and L shoulder in 2002
while working previous job, and had visual disturbances since then. States he had SLAP repair L shoulder in 2014 and vein
procedure done on L arm, which was slightly successful, but still have significant weakness throughout LUE and limited motion L
shoulder. Have "blackouts" when turning head too quickly. Also been having intermittent radiating pain and N/T down LLE into
big toe. A good night sleep has been ~2 hours. Works as a baker. Very difficult driving due to neck rotation.
Patient has not been identified as a fall risk at the time of this evaluation.
Summary List: Significant Medical DX/Conditions: Present: Asthma, Back injury
Subjective Examination
Left Spine
Mechanism of Injury: MVA May 30 2024
Mini-open labral debridement 2014
100 lbs. dropped on head from >20 feet. in 2002
Rehabilitation Expectations/Goals: Minimize: Pain.
Chief Complaint: Pain: Severity:
Current 9/10
At Best 9/10
At Worst 9/10
ADL / Functional Status:
Premorbid Status: ADL/ IADL: Independent Without Difficulty.
Current Status: ADL/ IADL: Activities:
Carrying unable to use LUE
Driving/Traveling Painful turning head
Housework- Heavy Unable to Perform
Sitting Increases back pain
Standing Increases back pain after extended period of time
Daily Comments: 9/23: Pt. states had slight increased pain since last visit, but it was already high to begin with. Heat gives
temporary pain relief.
10/2: Pt. states he's not sleeping much.
10/4: Pt. states if he sleeps in recliner, he wakes up with a severe muscle spasm in neck. Can't get comfortable in bed either.
10/9: Pt. states he had another event in past few days during which he turned quickly and legs gave out on him.
10/11: Pt. states LBP is mostly left-sided and at times radiates down LLE. This can occur with quick rotation or prolonged sitting.
10/18: Pt. states neck feels extremely tight. Pain never goes away.

Left Spine

Diagnoses
Daily Note 
Left M54.12 Radiculopathy, cervical region
Spine
M54.16 Radiculopathy, lumbar region
M54.6 Pain in thoracic spine
General Information
Pt. reports being involved in MVA May 30 during which he was hit on the side by an ambulance. States he had pre-existing issues
with L shoulder and neck/LUE, and this exacerbated symptoms greatly. Had 100 lbs. land on his head and L shoulder in 2002
while working previous job, and had visual disturbances since then. States he had SLAP repair L shoulder in 2014 and vein
procedure done on L arm, which was slightly successful, but still have significant weakness throughout LUE and limited motion L
shoulder. Have "blackouts" when turning head too quickly. Also been having intermittent radiating pain and N/T down LLE into
big toe. A good night sleep has been ~2 hours. Works as a baker. Very difficult driving due to neck rotation.
Patient has not been identified as a fall risk at the time of this evaluation.
Summary List: Significant Medical DX/Conditions: Present: Asthma, Back injury
Subjective Examination
Left Spine
Mechanism of Injury: MVA May 30 2024
Mini-open labral debridement 2014
100 lbs. dropped on head from >20 feet. in 2002
Rehabilitation Expectations/Goals: Minimize: Pain.
Chief Complaint: Pain: Severity:
 • Current 9/10
 • At Best 9/10
 • At Worst 9/10
ADL / Functional Status:
 • Premorbid Status: ADL/ IADL: Independent Without Difficulty.
 • Current Status: ADL/ IADL: Activities:
 • Carrying unable to use LUE
 • Driving/Traveling Painful turning head
 • Housework- Heavy Unable to Perform
 • Sitting Increases back pain
 • Standing Increases back pain after extended period of time
Daily Comments: 9/23: Pt. states had slight increased pain since last visit, but it was already high to begin with. Heat gives
temporary pain relief.
10/2: Pt. states he's not sleeping much.
10/4: Pt. states if he sleeps in recliner, he wakes up with a severe muscle spasm in neck. Can't get comfortable in bed either.
10/9: Pt. states he had another event in past few days during which he turned quickly and legs gave out on him.
10/11: Pt. states LBP is mostly left-sided and at times radiates down LLE. This can occur with quick rotation or prolonged sitting.
10/18: Pt. states neck feels extremely tight. Pain never goes away.
10/23: Pt. states he didn't sleep at all last night.

Left Spine

Daily Note 
Left M54.12 Radiculopathy, cervical region
Spine
M54.16 Radiculopathy, lumbar region
M54.6 Pain in thoracic spine
General Information
Pt. reports being involved in MVA May 30 during which he was hit on the side by an ambulance. States he had pre-existing issues
with L shoulder and neck/LUE, and this exacerbated symptoms greatly. Had 100 lbs. land on his head and L shoulder in 2002
while working previous job, and had visual disturbances since then. States he had SLAP repair L shoulder in 2014 and vein
procedure done on L arm, which was slightly successful, but still have significant weakness throughout LUE and limited motion L
shoulder. Have "blackouts" when turning head too quickly. Also been having intermittent radiating pain and N/T down LLE into
big toe. A good night sleep has been ~2 hours. Works as a baker. Very difficult driving due to neck rotation.
Patient has not been identified as a fall risk at the time of this evaluation.
Summary List: Significant Medical DX/Conditions: Present: Asthma, Back injury
Subjective Examination
Left Spine
Mechanism of Injury: MVA May 30 2024
Mini-open labral debridement 2014
100 lbs. dropped on head from >20 feet. in 2002
Rehabilitation Expectations/Goals: Minimize: Pain.
Chief Complaint: Pain: Severity:
 • Current 9/10
 • At Best 9/10
 • At Worst 9/10
ADL / Functional Status:
 • Premorbid Status: ADL/ IADL: Independent Without Difficulty.
 • Current Status: ADL/ IADL: Activities:
 • Carrying unable to use LUE
 • Driving/Traveling Painful turning head
 • Housework- Heavy Unable to Perform
 • Sitting Increases back pain
 • Standing Increases back pain after extended period of time
Daily Comments: 9/23: Pt. states had slight increased pain since last visit, but it was already high to begin with. Heat gives
temporary pain relief.
10/2: Pt. states he's not sleeping much.
10/4: Pt. states if he sleeps in recliner, he wakes up with a severe muscle spasm in neck. Can't get comfortable in bed either.
10/9: Pt. states he had another event in past few days during which he turned quickly and legs gave out on him.
10/11: Pt. states LBP is mostly left-sided and at times radiates down LLE. This can occur with quick rotation or prolonged sitting.
10/18: Pt. states neck feels extremely tight. Pain never goes away.
10/23: Pt. states he didn't sleep at all last night.
11/4: Pt. states MD office hasn't received PT notes.
Objective Examination
Left Spine
Posture: Forward Head/Rounded Shoulders: Slight.

Pt. reports being involved in MVA May 30 during which he was hit on the side by an ambulance. States he had pre-existing issues
with L shoulder and neck/LUE, and this exacerbated symptoms greatly. Had 100 lbs. land on his head and L shoulder in 2002
while working previous job, and had visual disturbances since then. States he had SLAP repair L shoulder in 2014 and vein
procedure done on L arm, which was slightly successful, but still have significant weakness throughout LUE and limited motion L
shoulder. Have "blackouts" when turning head too quickly. Also been having intermittent radiating pain and N/T down LLE into
big toe. A good night sleep has been ~2 hours. Works as a baker. Very difficult driving due to neck rotation.
Patient has not been identified as a fall risk at the time of this evaluation.
Summary List: Significant Medical DX/Conditions: Present: Asthma, Back injury

Left Spine

Mini-open labral debridement 2014

Evaluation Components: Jimmy Ferguson has attended 12 treatment sessions including evaluation for acute exacerbation of

LLE pain and N/T. Not reporting a significant improvement in neck pain, but fair improvement in back pain. No recent episodes of
"blackouts." Fair improvement in B hip strength and L shoulder strength in neutral.
The patient was educated regarding their diagnosis, prognosis, related pathology & plan of care. The patient demonstrates a
good understanding of the risks, benefits, precautions/contraindications, & prognosis of their skilled rehabilitation program.

M54.6 Pain in thoracic spine
General Information
Pt. reports being involved in MVA May 30 during which he was hit on the side by an ambulance. States he had pre-existing issues
with L shoulder and neck/LUE, and this exacerbated symptoms greatly. Had 100 lbs. land on his head and L shoulder in 2002
while working previous job, and had visual disturbances since then. States he had SLAP repair L shoulder in 2014 and vein
procedure done on L arm, which was slightly successful, but still have significant weakness throughout LUE and limited motion L
shoulder. Have "blackouts" when turning head too quickly. Also been having intermittent radiating pain and N/T down LLE into
big toe. A good night sleep has been ~2 hours. Works as a baker. Very difficult driving due to neck rotation.
Patient has not been identified as a fall risk at the time of this evaluation.

General Information
Pt. reports being involved in MVA May 30 during which he was hit on the side by an ambulance. States he had pre-existing issues
with L shoulder and neck/LUE, and this exacerbated symptoms greatly. Had 100 lbs. land on his head and L shoulder in 2002
while working previous job, and had visual disturbances since then. States he had SLAP repair L shoulder in 2014 and vein
procedure done on L arm, which was slightly successful, but still have significant weakness throughout LUE and limited motion L
shoulder. Have "blackouts" when turning head too quickly. Also been having intermittent radiating pain and N/T down LLE into
big toe. A good night sleep has been ~2 hours. Works as a baker. Very difficult driving due to neck rotation.
Patient has not been identified as a fall risk at the time of this evaluation.

Assessment
Evaluation Components: Jimmy Ferguson has attended 14 treatment sessions including evaluation for acute exacerbation of
chronic neck pain with LUE weakness, and chronic L shoulder pain onset MVA 5/30/24. Also having c/o acute LBP with radiating
LLE pain and N/T. Since previous re-evaluation 11/8/24, demonstrating fair improvement in C-spine rotation bilaterally. Remains
significantly limited with C-spine extension and had one "blackout" in this time, triggered by quick head turning while driving. No
change in LUE strength or grip strength. C-spine MRI scheduled 12/20/24. Plan to hold PT until this time.
Recommendations: Skilled Intervention: Required To: Decrease Pain.
The patient was educated regarding their diagnosis, prognosis, related pathology & plan of care. The patient demonstrates a
good understanding of the risks, benefits, precautions/contraindications, & prognosis of their skilled rehabilitation program.
Recommendations: Skilled Intervention:
 • Required To: Improve Balance. Improve Function. Improve Motor Control.

Assessment
Evaluation Components: Jimmy Ferguson has attended 14 treatment sessions including evaluation for acute exacerbation of
chronic neck pain with LUE weakness, and chronic L shoulder pain onset MVA 5/30/24. Also having c/o acute LBP with radiating
LLE pain and N/T. Since previous re-evaluation 11/8/24, demonstrating fair improvement in C-spine rotation bilaterally. Remains
significantly limited with C-spine extension and had one "blackout" in this time, triggered by quick head turning while driving. No
change in LUE strength or grip strength. C-spine MRI scheduled 12/20/24. Plan to hold PT until this time.
Recommendations: Skilled Intervention: Required To: Decrease Pain.
The patient was educated regarding their diagnosis, prognosis, related pathology & plan of care. The patient demonstrates a
good understanding of the risks, benefits, precautions/contraindications, & prognosis of their skilled rehabilitation program.
Recommendations: Skilled Intervention:
 • Required To: Improve Balance. Improve Function. Improve Motor Control.
